in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc3\xa6o\xcc\xaf</span></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">e</span>\n</th>\n<td></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ei\xcc\xaf</span></td>\n<td></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">eu\xcc\xaf</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">i</span>\n</th>\n<td></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ii\xcc\xaf</span></td>\n<td></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">iu\xcc\xaf</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">o</span>\n</th>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">oe\xcc\xaf</span></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">oi\xcc\xaf</span></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">oo\xcc\xaf</span></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ou\xcc\xaf</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">u</span>\n</th>\n<td></td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ui\xcc\xaf</span></td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stress">Stress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Stress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In standard Bengali, <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">stress</a> is predominantly initial. Bengali words are virtually all <a href="/wiki/Trochee" title="Trochee">trochaic</a>; the primary stress falls on the initial <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllable</a> of the word, while secondary stress often falls on all odd-numbered syllables thereafter, giving strings such as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa6\xb9\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa7\x8b\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <i><b>sh\xc3\xb4</b>-h\xc3\xb4-<b>jo</b>-gi-<b>ta</b></i> "cooperation", where the <b>boldface</b> represents primary and secondary stress.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonant_clusters">Consonant clusters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Consonant clusters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_consonant_clusters" title="Bengali consonant clusters">Bengali consonant clusters</a></div>\n<p>Native Bengali words do not allow initial <a href="/wiki/Consonant_cluster" title="Consonant cluster">consonant clusters</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> the maximum syllabic structure is CVC (i.e. one vowel flanked by a consonant on each side). Many speakers of Bengali restrict their phonology to this pattern, even when using Sanskrit or English borrowings, such as <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xae</span> <i>geram</i> (CV.CVC) for <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xae</span> <i>gram</i> (CCVC) "village" or <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x87\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2</span> <i>iskul</i> (VC.CVC) for <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2</span> <i>skul</i> (CCVC) "school".\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">Writing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Writing system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali alphabet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Braille" title="Bengali Braille">Bengali Braille</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg/220px-Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg" width="220" height="416" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg/330px-Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="354" data-file-height="669" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of handwritten Bengali. Part of a poem written in Bengali (and with its English translation below each Bengali paragraph) by Nobel Laureate <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a> in 1926 in Hungary</div></div></div>\n<p>The Bengali script is an <a href="/wiki/Abugida" title="Abugida">abugida</a>, a script with letters for consonants, diacritics for vowels, and in which an <a href="/wiki/Inherent_vowel" title="Inherent vowel">inherent vowel</a> (\xe0\xa6\x85 <i>\xc3\xb4</i>) is assumed for consonants if no vowel is marked.<sup id="cite_ref-it46_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-it46-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The Bengali alphabet is used throughout Bangladesh and eastern India (Assam, West Bengal, Tripura). The Bengali alphabet is believed to have evolved from a modified <a href="/wiki/Brahmic_scripts" title="Brahmic scripts">Brahmic script</a> around 1000 CE (or 10th \xe2\x80\x93 11th century).<sup id="cite_ref-akhor_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akhor-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Note that despite Bangladesh being majority Muslim, it uses the Bengali alphabet rather than an <a href="/wiki/Arabic_alphabet" title="Arabic alphabet">Arabic-based one</a> like the <a href="/wiki/Shahmukhi_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Shahmukhi script">Shahmukhi script</a> used in Pakistan.\n</p><p>The Bengali script is a <a href="/wiki/Cursive" title="Cursive">cursive</a> script with eleven <a href="/wiki/Grapheme" title="Grapheme">graphemes</a> or signs denoting nine vowels and two <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongs</a>, and thirty-nine graphemes representing <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">consonants</a> and other modifiers.<sup id="cite_ref-akhor_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akhor-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> There are no distinct <a href="/wiki/Letter_case" title="Letter case">upper and lower case</a> letter forms. The letters run from left to right and spaces are used to separate <a href="/wiki/Word#Orthography" title="Word">orthographic words</a>. Bengali script has a distinctive horizontal line running along the tops of the graphemes that links them together called <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <i>matra</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the Bengali script is an abugida, its consonant graphemes usually do not represent phonetic <a href="/wiki/Segment_(linguistics)" title="Segment (linguistics)">segments</a>, but carry an "inherent" vowel and thus are <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllabic</a> in nature. The inherent vowel is usually a back vowel, either <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x94]</span> as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xa4</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[m<b>\xc9\x94</b>t\xcc\xaa]</span> "opinion" or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[o]</span>, as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[m<b>o</b>n]</span> "mind", with variants like the more open <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x92]</span>. To emphatically represent a consonant sound without any inherent vowel attached to it, a special diacritic, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Virama" title="Virama">h\xc3\xb4s\xc3\xb4nt\xc3\xb4</a></i> <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">(\xe0\xa7\x8d)</span>, may be added below the basic consonant grapheme (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x8d</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[m]</span>). This diacritic, however, is not common, and is chiefly employed as a guide to pronunciation. The abugida nature of Bengali consonant graphemes is not consistent, however. Often, syllable-final consonant graphemes, though not marked by a <i>h\xc3\xb4s\xc3\xb4nt\xc3\xb4</i>, may carry no inherent vowel sound (as in the final <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[m<b>o</b>n]</span> or the medial <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae</span> in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa1amla]</span>).\n</p><p>A consonant sound followed by some vowel sound other than the inherent <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x94]</span> is orthographically realized by using a variety of vowel <a href="/wiki/Allography" title="Allography">allographs</a> above, below, before, after, or around the consonant sign, thus forming the ubiquitous consonant-vowel <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">typographic ligatures</a>. These allographs, called <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb0</span> <i>kar</i>, are <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritical</a> vowel forms and cannot stand on their own. For example, the graph <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xbf</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mi]</span> represents the consonant <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[m]</span> followed by the vowel <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i]</span>, where <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i]</span> is represented as the diacritical allograph<span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xbf</span> (called <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x87-\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb0</span> <i>i-kar</i>) and is placed <i>before</i> the default consonant sign. Similarly, the graphs <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ma]</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x80</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mi]</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x81</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mu]</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x82</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mu]</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x83</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mri]</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x87</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[me~m\xc3\xa6]</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x88</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[moj]</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x8b</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mo]</span> and <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x8c</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mow]</span> represent the same consonant <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae</span> combined with seven other vowels and two diphthongs. In these consonant-vowel ligatures, the so-called "inherent" vowel <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x94]</span> is first expunged from the consonant before adding the vowel, but this intermediate expulsion of the inherent vowel is not indicated in any visual manner on the basic consonant sign <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[m\xc9\x94]</span>.\n</p><p>The vowel graphemes in Bengali can take two forms: the independent form found in the basic inventory of the script and the dependent, abridged, allograph form (as discussed above). To represent a vowel in isolation from any preceding or following consonant, the independent form of the vowel is used. For example, in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\x87</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[moj]</span> "ladder" and in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x87\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xb6</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ili\xc9\x95]</span> "Hilsa fish", the independent form of the vowel <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x87</span> is used (cf. the dependent form<span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xbf)</span>. A vowel at the beginning of a word is always realized using its independent form.\n</p><p>In addition to the inherent-vowel-suppressing <i>h\xc3\xb4s\xc3\xb4nt\xc3\xb4</i>, three more diacritics are commonly used in Bengali. These are the superposed <i>ch\xc3\xb4ndr\xc3\xb4bindu</i> <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">(\xe0\xa6\x81)</span>, denoting a suprasegmental for <a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">nasalization</a> of vowels (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x9a\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x81\xe0\xa6\xa6</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t\xc9\x95\xc3\xa3d]</span> "moon"), the postposed <i>\xc3\xb4nusbar</i> <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">(\xe0\xa6\x82)</span> indicating the <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">velar nasal</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc5\x8b]</span> (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x82\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ba\xc5\x8bla]</span> "Bengali") and the postposed <i>bis\xc3\xb4rg\xc3\xb4</i> <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">(\xe0\xa6\x83)</span> indicating the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">voiceless glottal fricative</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[h]</span> (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x89\xe0\xa6\x83!</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[uh]</span> "ouch!") or the <a href="/wiki/Gemination" title="Gemination">gemination</a> of the following consonant (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa6\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\x83\xe0\xa6\x96</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[duk\xca\xb0\xcb\x90\xc9\x94]</span> "sorrow").\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bengali_consonant_clusters" title="Bengali consonant clusters">Bengali consonant clusters</a> (<span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\x9e\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> <i>jukt\xc3\xb4b\xc3\xaanj\xc3\xb4n</i>) are usually realized as ligatures, where the consonant which comes first is put on top of or to the left of the one that immediately follows. In these ligatures, the shapes of the constituent consonant signs are often contracted and sometimes even distorted beyond recognition. In the Bengali writing system, there are nearly 285 such ligatures denoting consonant clusters. Although there exist <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet#Consonant_conjuncts" title="Bengali alphabet">a few visual formulas</a> to construct some of these ligatures, many of them have to be learned by rote. Recently, in a bid to lessen this burden on young learners, efforts have been made by educational institutions in the two main Bengali-speaking regions (West Bengal and Bangladesh) to address the opaque nature of many consonant clusters, and as a result, modern Bengali textbooks are beginning to contain more and more "transparent" graphical forms of consonant clusters, in which the constituent consonants of a cluster are readily apparent from the graphical form. However, since this change is not as widespread and is not being followed as uniformly in the rest of the Bengali printed literature, today\'s Bengali-learning children will possibly have to learn to recognize both the new "transparent" and the old "opaque" forms, which ultimately amounts to an increase in learning burden.\n</p><p>Bengali punctuation marks, apart from the downstroke <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa5\xa4</span> <i>da\xe1\xb9\x9bi</i> \xe2\x80\x93 the Bengali equivalent of a <a href="/wiki/Full_stop" title="Full stop">full stop</a> \xe2\x80\x93 have been adopted from western scripts and their usage is similar.<sup id="cite_ref-huq_sarkar_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huq_sarkar-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Unlike in western scripts (Latin, Cyrillic, etc.) where the letter-forms stand on an invisible baseline, the Bengali letter-forms instead hang from a visible horizontal left-to-right headstroke called <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <i>matra</i>. The presence and absence of this matra can be important. For example, the letter <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa4</span> <i>t\xc3\xb4</i> and the numeral <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa7\xa9</span> "3" are distinguishable only by the presence or absence of the <i>matra</i>, as is the case between the consonant cluster <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0</span> <i>tr\xc3\xb4</i> and the independent vowel <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x8f</span> <i>e</i>. The letter-forms also employ the concepts of letter-width and letter-height (the vertical space between the visible matra and an invisible baseline).\n</p><p>There is yet to be a uniform standard <a href="/wiki/Collating_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Collating sequence">collating sequence</a> (sorting order of graphemes to be used in dictionaries, indices, computer sorting programs, etc.) of Bengali graphemes. Experts in both Bangladesh and India are currently working towards a common solution for this problem.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthographic_depth">Orthographic depth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Orthographic depth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Bengali script in general has a comparatively <a href="/wiki/Orthographic_depth" title="Orthographic depth">shallow orthography</a>, i.e., in most cases there is a one-to-one correspondence between the sounds (phonemes) and the letters (graphemes) of Bengali. But grapheme-phoneme inconsistencies do occur in certain cases.\n</p><p>One kind of inconsistency is due to the presence of several letters in the script for the same sound. In spite of some modifications in the 19th century, the Bengali spelling system continues to be based on the one used for Sanskrit,<sup id="cite_ref-huq_sarkar_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huq_sarkar-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and thus does not take into account some sound mergers that have occurred in the spoken language. For example, there are three letters (<span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb6</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb7</span>, and <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8</span>) for the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolo-palatal_sibilant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless alveolo-palatal sibilant">voiceless alveolo-palatal sibilant</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x95\xc9\x94]</span>, although the letter <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8</span> retains the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless alveolar sibilant">voiceless alveolar sibilant</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[s\xc9\x94]</span> sound when used in certain consonant conjuncts as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\x96\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[sk\xca\xb0\xc9\x94l\xc9\x94n]</span> "fall", <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xaa\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xa6\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[sp\xc9\x94nd\xc9\x94n]</span> "beat", etc. The letter <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb7</span> also retains the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_sibilant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless retroflex sibilant">voiceless retroflex sibilant</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x82\xc9\x94]</span> sound when used in certain consonant conjuncts as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xb7\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\x9f</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[k\xc9\x94\xca\x82\xca\x88\xc9\x94]</span> "suffering", <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x8b\xe0\xa6\xb7\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xa0\xe0\xa7\x80</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa1o\xca\x82\xca\x88\xca\xb0i]</span> "clan", etc. Similarly, there are two letters (<span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x9c</span> and <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xaf</span>) for the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_affricate" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal affricate">voiced alveolo-palatal affricate</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[d\xca\x91\xc9\x94]</span>. Moreover, what was once pronounced and written as a retroflex nasal <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa3</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xb3\xc9\x94]</span> is now pronounced as an alveolar <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[n\xc9\x94]</span> when in conversation (the difference is seen heard when reading) (unless conjoined with another <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_consonant" title="Retroflex consonant">retroflex consonant</a> such as <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x9f</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa0</span>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa1</span> and <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa2</span>), although the spelling does not reflect this change. The <a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">near-open front unrounded vowel</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6]</span> is orthographically realized by multiple means, as seen in the following examples: <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x8f\xe0\xa6\xa4</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6t\xc9\x94]</span> "so much", <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x8f\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa1\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa7\x80</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6kademi]</span> "academy", <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x85\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6miba]</span> "amoeba", <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa6\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\x96\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[d\xc3\xa6k\xca\xb0a]</span> "to see", <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xa4</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[b\xc3\xa6st\xc9\x94]</span> "busy", <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xa3</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[b\xc3\xa6k\xc9\x94r\xc9\x94n]</span> "grammar".\n</p><p>Another kind of inconsistency is concerned with the incomplete coverage of phonological information in the script. The inherent vowel attached to every consonant can be either <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x94]</span> or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[o]</span> depending on <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">vowel harmony</a> (<span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa6\x99\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbf</span>) with the preceding or following vowel or on the context, but this phonological information is not captured by the script, creating ambiguity for the reader. Furthermore, the inherent vowel is often not pronounced at the end of a syllable, as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xae</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[k\xc9\x94m]</span> "less", but this omission is not generally reflected in the script, making it difficult for the new reader.\n</p><p>Many consonant clusters have different sounds than their constituent consonants. For example, the combination of the consonants <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[k]</span> and <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb7</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x82\xc9\x94]</span> is graphically realized as <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb7</span> and is pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[kk\xca\xb0\xc9\x94]</span> (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb7</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[rukk\xca\xb0\xc9\x94]</span> "rugged") or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[kk\xca\xb0o]</span> (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb7\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbf</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[kk\xca\xb0ot\xcc\xaai]</span> "loss") or even <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[kk\xca\xb0\xc9\x94]</span> (as in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb7\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[kk\xca\xb0\xc9\x94m\xc9\x94t\xcc\xaaa]</span> "power"), depending on the position of the cluster in a word. The Bengali writing system is, therefore, not always a true guide to pronunciation.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The script used for Bengali, Assamese and other languages is known as Bengali-Assamese or <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Nagari_script" title="Eastern Nagari script">Eastern Nagari script</a>. The script is known as the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali alphabet</a> for Bengali and its dialects and the <a href="/wiki/Assamese_alphabet" title="Assamese alphabet">Assamese alphabet</a> for <a href="/wiki/Assamese_language" title="Assamese language">Assamese language</a> with some minor variations. Other related languages in the nearby region also make use of the Bengali alphabet like the <a href="/wiki/Meitei_language" title="Meitei language">Meitei language</a> in the Indian state of <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a>, where the Meitei language has been written in the Bengali alphabet for centuries, though the <a href="/wiki/Meitei_script" title="Meitei script">Meitei script</a> has been promoted in recent times.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romanisation">Romanisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Romanisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romanisation_of_Bengali" title="Romanisation of Bengali">Romanisation of Bengali</a></div>\n<p>There are various ways of Romanisation systems of Bengali created in recent years which have failed to represent the true Bengali phonetic sound. The Bengali alphabet has often been included with the group of Brahmic scripts for romanisation where the true phonetic value of Bengali is never represented. Some of them are the <a href="/wiki/International_Alphabet_of_Sanskrit_Transliteration" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration</a> or IAST system (based on diacritics),<sup id="cite_ref-IAST1_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAST1-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> "Indian languages Transliteration" or <a href="/wiki/ITRANS" title="ITRANS">ITRANS</a> (uses upper case letters suited for <a href="/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">ASCII</a> keyboards),<sup id="cite_ref-ITRANS1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITRANS1-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_at_Kolkata_romanisation" title="National Library at Kolkata romanisation">National Library at Kolkata romanization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NatLib_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatLib-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the context of Bengali <a href="/wiki/Romanization" title="Romanization">romanisation</a>, it is important to distinguish <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliteration</a> from <a href="/wiki/Transcription_(linguistics)" title="Transcription (linguistics)">transcription</a>. Transliteration is orthographically accurate (i.e. the original spelling can be recovered), whereas transcription is phonetically accurate (the pronunciation can be reproduced).\n</p><p>Although it might be desirable to use a transliteration scheme where the original Bengali orthography is recoverable from the Latin text, Bengali words are currently Romanized on Wikipedia using a <a href="/wiki/Phonemic_orthography" title="Phonemic orthography">phonemic transcription</a>, where the true phonetic pronunciation of Bengali is represented with no reference to how it is written.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Grammar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_grammar" title="Bengali grammar">Bengali grammar</a></div>\n<p>Bengali nouns are not assigned gender, which leads to minimal changing of adjectives (<a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">inflection</a>). However, nouns and pronouns are moderately <a href="/wiki/Declension" title="Declension">declined</a> (altered depending on their function in a sentence) into four <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">cases</a> while verbs are heavily <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_conjugation" title="Grammatical conjugation">conjugated</a>, and the verbs do not change form depending on the gender of the nouns.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Word order">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Head-directionality_parameter" title="Head-directionality parameter">head-final</a> language, Bengali follows <a href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93object%E2%80%93verb" title="Subject\xe2\x80\x93object\xe2\x80\x93verb">subject\xe2\x80\x93object\xe2\x80\x93verb</a> <a href="/wiki/Word_order" title="Word order">word order</a>, although variations to this theme are common.<sup id="cite_ref-tb16_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tb16-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Bengali makes use of <a href="/wiki/Preposition_and_postposition" title="Preposition and postposition">postpositions</a>, as opposed to the prepositions used in English and other European languages. <a href="/wiki/Determiner" title="Determiner">Determiners</a> follow the <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">noun</a>, while numerals, <a href="/wiki/Adjective" title="Adjective">adjectives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Possession_(linguistics)" title="Possession (linguistics)">possessors</a> precede the noun.<sup id="cite_ref-UCLA1_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLA1-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Yes-no questions do not require any change to the basic word order; instead, the low (L) <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tone</a> of the final syllable in the utterance is replaced with a falling (HL) tone. Additionally, optional <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_particle" title="Grammatical particle">particles</a> (e.g. <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xbf</span> <i>-ki</i>, <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <i>-na</i>, etc.) are often <a href="/wiki/Clitic" title="Clitic">encliticized</a> onto the first or last word of a yes-no question.\n</p><p>Wh-questions are formed by fronting the wh-word to <a href="/wiki/Focus_(linguistics)" title="Focus (linguistics)">focus</a> position, which is typically the first or second word in the utterance.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns">Nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Nouns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Nouns and pronouns are inflected for <a href="/wiki/Declension" title="Declension">case</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Nominative_case" title="Nominative case">nominative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">objective</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive (possessive)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Locative_case" title="Locative case">locative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tb_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tb-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The case marking pattern for each noun being inflected depends on the noun\'s degree of <a href="/wiki/Animacy" title="Animacy">animacy</a>. When a <a href="/wiki/Article_(grammar)" title="Article (grammar)">definite article</a> such as <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">-\xe0\xa6\x9f\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <i>-\xe1\xb9\xada</i> (singular) or <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">-\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa7\x8b</span> <i>-gulo</i> (plural) is added, as in the tables below, nouns are also inflected for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">number</a>.\n</p><p>In most of the Bengali grammar books, cases are divided in to 6 categories and an additional possessive case (possessive form is not recognized as a type of case by Bengali grammarian). But in term of usages, cases are generally grouped in to only 4 categories.\n</p>\n<table style="align:center; width:60%; margin:1em auto 1em auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr valign="top">\n<td>\n<table students\n</td>\n<td><span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xbe/\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x8b\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa7\x8b<b>\xe0\xa6\xb0</b></span><br /> juta-gula/juto-gulo-<b>r</b><br />the shoes\'\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Locative\n</th>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td><span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xbe/\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x8b\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa7\x8b<b>\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x87</b></span><br />juta-gula/juto-gulo-<b>te</b><br />on/in the shoes\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>When counted, nouns take one of a small set of <a href="/wiki/Measure_word" title="Measure word">measure words</a>. Similar to Japanese, the nouns in Bengali cannot be counted by adding the numeral directly adjacent to the noun. The noun\'s measure word (<b>MW</b>) must be used between the numeral and the noun. Most nouns take the generic measure word <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">-\xe0\xa6\x9f\xe0\xa6\xbe</span> <i>-\xe1\xb9\xada</i>, though other measure words indicate semantic classes (e.g. <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">-\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> <i>-j\xc3\xb4n</i> for humans). There is also the classifier <i>-khana,</i> and its diminutive form <i>-khani</i>, which only attach to nouns which are flat, long, square, or thin. These are the least common of the classifiers.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto">\n\n<caption>Measure words\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Bengali\n</th>\n<th>Bengali transliteration\n</th>\n<th>Literal translation\n</th>\n<th>English translation\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbc<b>\xe0\xa6\x9f\xe0\xa6\xbe</b> \xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa7\x81</span>\n</td>\n<td>N\xc3\xb4y-<b>\xe1\xb9\xada</b> goru\n</td>\n<td>Nine-<b>MW</b> cow\n</td>\n<td>Nine cows\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbc<b>\xe0\xa6\x9f\xe0\xa6\xbe</b> \xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xb6</span>\n</td>\n<td>K\xc3\xb4y-<b>\xe1\xb9\xada</b> balish\n</td>\n<td>How many-<b>MW</b> pillow\n</td>\n<td>How many pillows\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x85\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\x95<b>\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xa8</b> \xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa7\x8b\xe0\xa6\x95</span>\n</td>\n<td>\xc3\x94nek-<b>j\xc3\xb4n</b> lok\n</td>\n<td>Many-<b>MW</b> person\n</td>\n<td>Many people\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x9a\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb0-\xe0\xa6\xaa\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x81\xe0\xa6\x9a<b>\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xa8</b> \xe0\xa6\xb6\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb7\xe0\xa6\x95</span>\n</td>\n<td>Car-p\xc3\xa3c-<b>j\xc3\xb4n</b> shikkh\xc3\xb4k\n</td>\n<td>Four-five-<b>MW</b> teacher\n</td>\n<td>Four or five teachers\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Measuring nouns in Bengali without their corresponding measure words (e.g. <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x86\xe0\xa6\x9f \xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xa1\xe0\xa6\xbc\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb2</span> <i>a\xe1\xb9\xad bi\xe1\xb9\x9bal</i> instead of <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\x86\xe0\xa6\x9f<b>\xe0\xa6\x9f\xe0\xa6\xbe</b> \xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xa1\xe0\xa6\xbc\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb2</span> <i>a\xe1\xb9\xad-<b>\xe1\xb9\xada</b> bi\xe1\xb9\x9bal</i> "eight cats") would typically be considered ungrammatical. However, when the semantic class of the noun is understood from the measure word, the noun is often omitted and only the measure word is used, e.g. <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb6\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xa7\xe0\xa7\x81 \xe0\xa6\x8f\xe0\xa6\x95<b>\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xa8</b> \xe0\xa6\xa5\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa5\xa4</span> <i>Shudhu \xc3\xaak-<b>j\xc3\xb4n</b> thakbe.</i> (lit. "Only one-<b>MW</b> will remain.") would be understood to mean "Only one <b>person</b> will remain.", given the semantic class implicit in <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">-\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xa8</span> <i>-j\xc3\xb4n</i>.\n</p><p>In this sense, all nouns in Bengali, unlike most other Indo-European languages, are similar to <a href="/wiki/Mass_noun" title="Mass noun">mass nouns</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs">Verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Verbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are two classes of verbs: <a href="/wiki/Finite_verb" title="Finite verb">finite</a> and non-finite. Non-finite verbs have no inflection for tense or person, while finite verbs are fully inflected for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">person</a> (first, second, third), <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_tense" title="Grammatical tense">tense</a> (present, past, future), <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">aspect</a> (simple, perfect, progressive), and <a href="/wiki/Honorific" title="Honorific">honor</a> (intimate, familiar, and formal), but <i>not</i> for number. <a href="/wiki/Conditional_mood" title="Conditional mood">Conditional</a>, imperative, and other special inflections for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_mood" title="Grammatical mood">mood</a> can replace the tense and aspect suffixes. The number of inflections on many verb roots can total more than 200.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">Inflectional</a> suffixes in the <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">morphology</a> of Bengali vary from region to region, along with minor differences in <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntax</a>.\n</p><p>Bengali differs from most Indo-Aryan Languages in the <a href="/wiki/Zero_copula" title="Zero copula">zero copula</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Copula_(linguistics)" title="Copula (linguistics)">copula</a> or connective <i>be</i> is often missing in the present tense.<sup id="cite_ref-huq_sarkar_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huq_sarkar-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Thus, "he is a teacher" is <span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text">\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x87 \xe0\xa6\xb6\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb7\xe0\xa6\x95</span> <i>se shikkh\xc3\xb4k</i>, (literally "he teacher").<sup id="cite_ref-hacce-bangali_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hacce-bangali-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In this respect, Bengali is similar to Russian and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>. <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> grammar is also the closest to Bengali grammar.<sup id="cite_ref-hub1995_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hub1995-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bengali_Vocabulary2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bengali_Vocabulary2.png/250px-Bengali_Vocabulary2.png" width="250" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2f/Bengali_Vocabulary2.png 1.5x" data-file-width="282" data-file-height="280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bengali_Vocabulary2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sources of modern literary Bengali words<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFCC99; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;67% native</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #993300; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;25% Sanskrit reborrowings</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF6666; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;8% indigenous and foreign loans</div></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_vocabulary" title="Bengali vocabulary">Bengali vocabulary</a></div>\n<p>Bengali has as many as 100,000 separate words, of which 50,000 are considered <a href="/wiki/Tadbhava" title="Tadbhava">Tadbhavas</a>, 21,100 are <a href="/wiki/Tatsama" title="Tatsama">Tatsamas</a> and the remainder <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> from <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic</a> and other foreign languages.\n</p><p>However, these figures do not take into account the large proportion of archaic or highly technical words that are very rarely used. Furthermore, different dialects use more <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> vocabulary especially in different areas of Bangladesh and Muslim majority areas of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> also Hindus use more Sanskrit vocabulary than Muslims and while standard Bengali is based on the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_dialects" title="Bengali dialects">Nadia dialect</a> of spoken in the Hindu majority states of West Bengal, about 90% of Bengalis in Bangladesh (cca. 148 million) and 27% of Bengalis in West Bengal and 10% in Assam (cca. 36 million) are Muslim and speak a more "persio-arabised" version of Bengali instead of the more Sanskrit influenced Standard <a href="/wiki/Bengali_dialects" title="Bengali dialects">Nadia dialect</a>. The productive vocabulary used in modern literary works, in fact, is made up mostly (67%) of tadbhavas, while tatsamas comprise only 25% of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-bhoumick_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bhoumick-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bhoumick1_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bhoumick1-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Loanwords from non-Indic languages comprise the remaining 8% of the vocabulary used in modern <a href="/wiki/Bengali_literature" title="Bengali literature">Bengali literature</a>.\n</p><p>Because of centuries of contact with <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Europeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Persians" class="mw-redirect" title="Persians">Persians</a>, Bengali has absorbed numerous words from foreign languages, often totally integrating these borrowings into the core vocabulary.\n</p><p>The most common borrowings from foreign languages come from three different kinds of contact. After close contact with several indigenous Austroasiatic languages,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and later the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> invasion whose court language was Persian, numerous <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_language" title="Chagatai language">Chagatai</a>, Arabic, and Persian words were absorbed into the lexicon.<sup id="cite_ref-sas_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sas-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later, East Asian travelers and lately European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a> brought words from <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, French, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, and most significantly English during the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">colonial period</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sample text">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following is a sample text in Bengali of Article 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>:\n</p><p><b>Bengali in the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali alphabet</a></b>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span lang="bn" title="Bengali language text"><b>\xe0\xa6\xa7\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe \xe0\xa7\xa7:</b> \xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xa4 \xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb7 \xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa7\xe0\xa7\x80\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa6\xad\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa7\x87 \xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa8 \xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa6\xe0\xa6\xbe \xe0\xa6\x8f\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\x82 \xe0\xa6\x85\xe0\xa6\xa7\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xb0 \xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbc\xe0\xa7\x87 \xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xb9\xe0\xa6\xa3 \xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa5\xa4 \xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x81\xe0\xa6\xa6\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\xb0 \xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\x95 \xe0\xa6\x8f\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\x82 \xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xa6\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xa7\xe0\xa6\xbf \xe0\xa6\x86\xe0\xa6\x9b\xe0\xa7\x87; \xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x82 \xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\x87 \xe0\xa6\x8f\xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa7\x87 \xe0\xa6\x85\xe0\xa6\xaa\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\xb0 \xe0\xa6\xaa\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xbf \xe0\xa6\xad\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x83\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xb8\xe0\xa7\x81\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xad \xe0\xa6\xae\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa7\x8b\xe0\xa6\xad\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xac \xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xaf\xe0\xa6\xbc\xe0\xa7\x87 \xe0\xa6\x86\xe0\xa6\x9a\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xa3 \xe0\xa6\x95\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\xbe \xe0\xa6\x89\xe0\xa6\x9a\xe0\xa6\xbf\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa5\xa4</span></dd></dl>\n<p><b>Bengali in <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Bengali" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanization of Bengali">phonetic Romanization</a></b>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><b>Dhara \xc3\xaak:</b> S\xc3\xb4m\xc3\xb4st\xc3\xb4 manush shadhinbhabe s\xc3\xb4man m\xc3\xb4rjada eb\xc3\xb4ng \xc3\xb4dhikar niye j\xc3\xb4nm\xc3\xb4gr\xc3\xb4h\xc3\xb4n k\xc3\xb4re. T\xc3\xa3der bibek eb\xc3\xb4ng buddhi achhe; sut\xc3\xb4rang s\xc3\xb4k\xc3\xb4leri \xc3\xaake \xc3\xb4p\xc3\xb4rer pr\xc3\xb4ti bhratritt\xc3\xb4sul\xc3\xb4bh m\xc3\xb4nobhab niye ach\xc3\xb4r\xc3\xb4n k\xc3\xb4ra uchit.</dd></dl>\n<p><b>Bengali in the <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">International Phonetic Alphabet</a></b>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">d\xca\xb1ara \xc3\xa6k | \xca\x83\xc9\x94m\xc9\x94st\xc9\x94 manu\xca\x83 \xca\x83ad\xca\xb1inb\xca\xb1abe \xca\x83\xc9\x94man m\xc9\x94rd\xca\x92ada eb\xc9\x94\xc5\x8b \xc9\x94d\xca\xb1ikar nie\xcc\xafe d\xca\x92\xc9\x94nm\xc9\x94\xc9\xa1r\xc9\x94h\xc9\x94n k\xc9\x94re | t\xc3\xa3der bibek eb\xc9\x94\xc5\x8b budd\xca\xb1\xcb\x90i at\xca\x83\xca\xb0e | sut\xc9\x94ra\xc5\x8b s\xc9\x94k\xc9\x94leri \xc3\xa6ke \xc9\x94p\xc9\x94rer pr\xc9\x94ti b\xca\xb1ratrit\xcb\x90\xc9\x94sul\xc9\x94b\xca\xb1 m\xc9\x94nob\xca\xb1ab nie\xcc\xafe at\xca\x83\xc9\x94r\xc9\x94n k\xc9\x94ra ut\xca\x83it</span></dd></dl>\n<p><b>Gloss</b>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><b>Clause 1:</b> All human free-manner-in equal dignity and right taken birth-take do. Their reason and intelligence exist; therefore everyone-indeed one another\'s towards brotherhood-ly attitude taken conduct do should.</dd></dl>\n<p><b>Translation</b>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><b>Article 1:</b> All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They possess conscience and reason. Therefore, everyone should act in a spirit of brotherhood towards each other.</dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span This is viewed as ungrammatical by other speakers, and speakers of this variety are sometimes (humorously) referred as "hocche-Bangali".</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-hub1995-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-hub1995_78-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">\n<cite class="citation journal">H\xc3\xbcbschmannov\xc3\xa1, Milena (1995).
